class="infobox-header" style="background-color: #DDDDFF; color: black"><a href="/wiki/Runway" title="Runway"><span style="background-color: #DDDDFF; color:black;">Runways</span></a>\n</th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" class="infobox-full-data">\n<table style="width:100%; margin:-2px -1px -1px -1px; border-spacing:0;">\n\n<tbody><tr style="background-color: #e6e6ff">\n<th rowspan="2" style="width: 15%; colspan="2" class="infobox-header" style="background-color: #DDDDFF; color: black">Statistics (2019)</th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" class="infobox-full-data"><table class="infobox-subbox"><tbody><tr><th decoding="async" title="Decrease" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/17px-Decrease2.svg.png 1.5x, style="background-color: #eee"><td colspan="2" class="infobox-full-data"><div style="text-align: left;">Sources: UK <a href="/wiki/Aeronautical_Information_Publication" title="Aeronautical Information Publication">AIP</a> at <a href="/wiki/National_Air_Traffic_Services" class="mw-redirect" title="National Air Traffic Services">NATS</a><sup id="cite_ref-aip_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aip-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><br />Statistics from the <a href="/wiki/Civil_Aviation_Authority_(United_Kingdom)" title="Civil Aviation Authority (United Kingdom)">UK Civil Aviation Authority</a><sup id="cite_ref-stats_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stats-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Liverpool John Lennon Airport</b> (<a href="/wiki/IATA_airport_code" title="IATA airport code">IATA</a>: <b>LPL</b>, <a href="/wiki/ICAO_airport_code" title="ICAO airport code">ICAO</a>: <b>EGGP</b>) is an <a href="/wiki/International_airport" title="International airport">international airport</a> located in <a href="/wiki/Liverpool" title="Liverpool">Liverpool</a>, England. The airport is within the City of Liverpool on the banks of the estuary of the <a href="/wiki/River_Mersey" title="River Mersey">River Mersey</a> some 6.5 <a href="/wiki/Nautical_mile" title="Nautical mile">nautical miles</a> (12.0&#160;km; 7.5&#160;mi) south-east of <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_city_centre" title="Liverpool city centre">Liverpool city centre</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-aip_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aip-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> Scheduled <a href="/wiki/Domestic_market" title="Domestic market">domestic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">European</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Africa" title="North Africa">North African</a> and <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">Middle Eastern</a><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> services are operated from the airport. The airport comprises a single passenger <a href="/wiki/Airport_terminal" title="Airport terminal">terminal</a>, three general use <a href="/wiki/Hangar" title="Hangar">hangars</a>, a <a href="/wiki/FedEx_Express" title="FedEx Express">FedEx Express</a> <a href="/wiki/Courier" title="Courier">courier service</a> centre as well as a single runway which is 7,500&#160;ft (2,286&#160;m) in length, with the <a href="/wiki/Air_traffic_control" title="Air traffic control">control tower</a> south of the runway.\n</p><p>Originally called <b>Speke Airport</b>, and still called this locally by some people, the airport was renamed after Liverpudlian musician <a href="/wiki/John_Lennon" title="John Lennon">John Lennon</a> of <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles" title="The Beatles">the Beatles</a> in 2001. On the outbreak of <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, the airport was operated by the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Air_Force" title="Royal Air Force">RAF</a> and known as <b>RAF Speke</b>. Between 1997 and 2007, the facility was one of Europe\'s fastest-growing airports, increasing annual passenger numbers from 689,468 in 1997 to 5.47 million in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-stats_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stats-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Despite passenger numbers having decreased to just over 4.8 million in 2016, this was an 11.1% increase on the 2015 total. In 2019, the airport handled 5.05 million passengers, making it the 13th-busiest airport in the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toclevel-2 tocsection-8"><a href="#Future_expansion"><span class="tocnumber">1.7</span> <span class="toctext">Future expansion</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 aircraft movements</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-14"><a href="#Route_statistics"><span class="tocnumber">5.2</span> <span class="toctext">Route class="toclevel-2 tocsection-20"><a href="#Hotels"><span class="tocnumber">7.1</span> <span class="toctext">Hotels</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-21"><a class="toctext">Bibliography</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-24"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-25"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Liverpool_John_Lennon_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Imperial_Airways">Imperial Airways</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Liverpool_John_Lennon_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Imperial Airways">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Built in part of the grounds of <a href="/wiki/Speke_Hall" title="Speke Hall">Speke Hall</a>, Liverpool (Speke) Airport, as the airport was originally known, started scheduled flights in 1930 with a service by <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Airways" title="Imperial Airways">Imperial Airways</a> via <a href="/wiki/City_Airport_Manchester" class="mw-redirect" title="City Airport Manchester">Barton Aerodrome</a> near <a href="/wiki/Eccles,_Greater_Manchester" title="Eccles, Greater Manchester">Eccles</a>, <a href="/wiki/City_of_Salford" title="City of Salford">Salford</a> and <a href="/wiki/Castle_Bromwich_Aerodrome" title="Castle Bromwich Aerodrome">Castle Bromwich Aerodrome</a>, <a href="/wiki/Birmingham" title="Birmingham">Birmingham</a> to <a href="/wiki/Croydon_Airport" title="Croydon Airport">Croydon Airport</a> near London. The airport was officially opened on 1 July 1933.<sup id="cite_ref-liverpoolecho.co.uk_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-liverpoolecho.co.uk-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> By the late 1930s, air traffic from Liverpool was beginning to take off with increasing demand for <a href="/wiki/Irish_Sea" title="Irish Sea">Irish Sea</a> crossings, and a distinctive <a href="/wiki/Airport_terminal" title="Airport terminal">passenger terminal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Control_tower" class="mw-redirect" title="Control tower">control tower</a> and two large aircraft <a href="/wiki/Hangar" title="Hangar">hangars</a> were built.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Second_World_War">Second World War</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Liverpool_John_Lennon_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Second World War">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>At the beginning of 1937 <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_City_Council" title="Liverpool City Council">Liverpool City Council</a> leased between 70 and 110 acres of their Speke Estate on a 999-year lease to the <a href="/wiki/Air_Ministry" title="Air Ministry">Air Ministry</a>. The price included at all times the use of Speke Airport next to the shadow factory site. The <a href="/wiki/London,_Midland_and_Scottish_Railway" title="London, Midland and Scottish Railway">LMS Railway</a> provided a siding. Erection of the building was planned to take 30 weeks and when complete it would provide employment for more than 5,000 people. It was to be managed by <a href="/wiki/Rootes_Securities_Ltd" class="mw-redirect" title="Rootes Securities Ltd">Rootes Securities</a> on behalf of the Air Ministry. Work started Monday 15 February 1937.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During the <a href="/wiki/Second_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Second World War">Second World War</a>, Speke was requisitioned by the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Air_Force" title="Royal Air Force">Royal Air Force</a> and known as RAF Speke. <a href="/wiki/Rootes_Group" title="Rootes Group">Rootes</a> built in a "<a href="/wiki/British_shadow_factories" title="British shadow factories">shadow factory</a>" by the airport <a href="/wiki/Bristol_Blenheim" title="Bristol Blenheim">Bristol Blenheims</a> and 1,070 <a href="/wiki/Handley_Page_Halifax" title="Handley Page Halifax">Handley Page Halifax</a> bombers.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lockheed_Corporation" title="Lockheed Corporation">Lockheed Aircraft Corporation</a> assembled many types of planes at the airport, including <a href="/wiki/Lockheed_Hudson" title="Lockheed Hudson">Hudsons</a> and <a href="/wiki/North_American_P-51_Mustang" title="North American P-51 Mustang">Mustang fighters</a>, that had been shipped from the United States in parts to <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Liverpool" title="Port of Liverpool">Liverpool Docks</a>. The airport was also home to the <a href="/wiki/Merchant_Ship_Fighter_Unit" title="Merchant Ship Fighter Unit">Merchant Ship Fighter Unit</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-liverpoolecho.co.uk_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-liverpoolecho.co.uk-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 8 October 1940 (one day before John Lennon\'s birth), Speke was witness to what is thought to be the fastest air-to-air combat "kill" in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Britain" title="Battle of Britain">Battle of Britain</a> and possibly of all time. <a href="/wiki/Flight_Lieutenant" class="mw-redirect" title="Flight Lieutenant">Flight Lieutenant</a> Denys Gillam took off in his <a href="/wiki/Hawker_Hurricane" title="Hawker Hurricane">Hawker Hurricane</a> from Speke to be confronted by a <a href="/wiki/Junkers_Ju_88" title="Junkers Ju 88">Junkers 88</a> passing across him. He shot the Junkers down while his <a href="/wiki/Landing_gear" title="Landing gear">undercarriage</a> was still retracting, and, along with <a href="/wiki/Alois_Va%C5%A1%C3%A1tko" title="Alois Va\xc5\xa1\xc3\xa1tko">Alois Va\xc5\xa1\xc3\xa1tko</a> and Josef Stehl\xc3\xadk, all of <a href="/wiki/No._312_Squadron_RAF" class="mw-redirect" title="No. 312 Squadron RAF">312 Squadron</a>, was credited with the kill. The moment has been caught in a painting by Robert Taylor called <i>Fastest Victory</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ahfv_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ahfv-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Civil_airport">Civil airport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Liverpool_John_Lennon_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Civil airport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:THE_FORMER_TERMINAL_BUILDING_AT_SPEKE_AERODROME_NOW_THE_CROWNE_PLAZA_HOTEL_LIVERPOOL_JULY_2013_(9231676102).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/THE_FORMER_TERMINAL_BUILDING_AT_SPEKE_AERODROME_NOW_THE_CROWNE_PLAZA_HOTEL_LIVERPOOL_JULY_2013_%289231676102%29.jpg/220px-THE_FORMER_TERMINAL_BUILDING_AT_SPEKE_AERODROME_NOW_THE_CROWNE_PLAZA_HOTEL_LIVERPOOL_JULY_2013_%289231676102%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="141" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/THE_FORMER_TERMINAL_BUILDING_AT_SPEKE_AERODROME_NOW_THE_CROWNE_PLAZA_HOTEL_LIVERPOOL_JULY_2013_%289231676102%29.jpg/330px-THE_FORMER_TERMINAL_BUILDING_AT_SPEKE_AERODROME_NOW_THE_CROWNE_PLAZA_HOTEL_LIVERPOOL_JULY_2013_%289231676102%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/THE_FORMER_TERMINAL_BUILDING_AT_SPEKE_AERODROME_NOW_THE_CROWNE_PLAZA_HOTEL_LIVERPOOL_JULY_2013_%289231676102%29.jpg/440px-THE_FORMER_TERMINAL_BUILDING_AT_SPEKE_AERODROME_NOW_THE_CROWNE_PLAZA_HOTEL_LIVERPOOL_JULY_2013_%289231676102%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3749" data-file-height="2410" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:THE_FORMER_TERMINAL_BUILDING_AT_SPEKE_AERODROME_NOW_THE_CROWNE_PLAZA_HOTEL_LIVERPOOL_JULY_2013_(9231676102).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The old terminal building, used between the 1930s and 1986, now the <a href="/wiki/Crowne_Plaza_Liverpool_John_Lennon_Airport_Hotel" title="Crowne Plaza Liverpool John Lennon Airport Hotel">Crowne Plaza Liverpool John Lennon Airport Hotel</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Normal civil airline operations resumed after <a href="/wiki/Victory_in_Europe_Day" title="Victory in Europe Day">VE-day</a> and passengers increased from 50,000 in 1945 to 75,000 in 1948, remaining ahead of <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Airport" title="Manchester Airport">Manchester Airport</a>. Ownership by the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Aviation" title="Ministry of Aviation">Ministry of Aviation</a> proved to be a drag on the airport\'s progress thereafter and Manchester gained the lead from 1949, resulting in Liverpool\'s loss of the only <a href="/wiki/Ground-controlled_approach" title="Ground-controlled approach">ground-controlled radar approach</a> unit available to <a href="/wiki/North_West_England" title="North West England">North West</a> airports, further hampering operation.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>During the post-war years, Speke Airport hosted an annual air display in aid of the <a href="/wiki/Soldiers,_Sailors,_and_Air_Force_Association" class="mw-redirect" title="Soldiers, Sailors, and Air Force Association">Soldiers, Sailors, and Air Force Association</a>, a charity for veterans. The displays were immensely popular and attracted a huge crowd. On one such occasion on 21 May 1956, tragedy struck with the death of <a href="/wiki/Leo_Valentin" class="mw-redirect" title="Leo Valentin">L\xc3\xa9on Alfred Nicolas "L\xc3\xa9o" Valentin</a>, billed as the Birdman, when his balsa wood wings struck the opening of the aircraft from which he was exiting and he was hurtled into an uncontrollable spin. He attempted to deploy his emergency parachute, but it became entangled and \'Roman candled\', leaving Leo to fall to his death. The local newspaper headlined the story with "The world has been robbed of a daring personality." Ironically, a few years earlier Valentin had been attributed with discovering the free-fall stable position still used by sports parachutists today for safe deployment.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="New_runway">New runway</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Liverpool_John_Lennon_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: New runway">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The city took over control of the airport on 1 January 1961 and prepared development plans. In 1966, a new 7,500&#160;ft (2,286&#160;m) runway was opened by <a href="/wiki/Prince_Philip,_Duke_of_Edinburgh" title="Prince Philip, Duke of Edinburgh">Prince Philip</a> on a new site to the southeast of the existing airfield. It enabled the airport to be open for business around the clock and is in use to this day. Control of the airport transferred to <a href="/wiki/Merseyside_County_Council" title="Merseyside County Council">Merseyside County Council</a> from <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_City_Council" title="Liverpool City Council">Liverpool Corporation</a> in the mid-1970s and then, ten years later, to the five <a href="/wiki/Merseyside" title="Merseyside">Merseyside</a> councils following the abolition of Merseyside County Council. In 1982, <a href="/wiki/Pope_John_Paul_II%27s_visit_to_the_United_Kingdom" title="Pope John Paul II&#39;s visit to the United Kingdom">Pope John Paul II visited</a> and met crowds at the old Liverpool airport.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Old_Terminal_.281986.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Old_Terminal_(1986)">Old Terminal (1986)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Liverpool_John_Lennon_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Old Terminal (1986)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>A modern passenger terminal adjacent to the new runway opened in 1986 followed by the closure of the original 1930s building.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The original terminal building dating from the late 1930s, famously seen on early television footage with its terraces packed with <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles" title="The Beatles">Beatles</a> fans, was left derelict until converted into a hotel, opening in 2001, preserving its <a href="/wiki/Listed_building" title="Listed building">Grade II listed</a> <a href="/wiki/Art_Deco" title="Art Deco">Art Deco</a> style. It was part of the <a href="/wiki/Marriott_Hotels_%26_Resorts" title="Marriott Hotels &amp; Resorts">Marriott</a> chain of hotels, but is currently the <a href="/wiki/Crowne_Plaza_Liverpool_John_Lennon_Airport_Hotel" title="Crowne Plaza Liverpool John Lennon Airport Hotel">Crowne Plaza Liverpool John Lennon Airport Hotel</a> after a renovation in August 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-fola_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fola-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> The former <a href="/wiki/Airport_ramp" class="mw-redirect" title="Airport ramp">apron</a> of the terminal is also listed and retained in its original condition, although it is no longer connected to the airport or subject to airside access control. It is the home of several aircraft, including <a href="/wiki/BAe_Jetstream_41" class="mw-redirect" title="BAe Jetstream 41">BAe Jetstream 41</a> prototype G-JMAC and <a href="/wiki/Bristol_Britannia" title="Bristol Britannia">Bristol Britannia</a> G-ANCF, preserved by the Speke Aerodrome Heritage Group.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> The two art-deco-style <a href="/wiki/Hangar" title="Hangar">hangars</a> that flank the terminal and apron have also been converted for new uses: one is now a <a href="/wiki/David_Lloyd_(tennis)" title="David Lloyd (tennis)">David Lloyd</a> <a href="/wiki/Leisure_centre" title="Leisure centre">leisure centre</a>, the other the headquarters of the <a href="/wiki/Shop_Direct_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="Shop Direct Group">Shop Direct Group</a>, called Skyways House.<sup id="cite_ref-fola_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fola-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-marriott_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-marriott-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-jscb_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jscb-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-jgw_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jgw-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1990 the airport was privatised, with <a href="/wiki/British_Aerospace" title="British Aerospace">British Aerospace</a> taking a 76% shareholding in the new company. Subsequently, the airport has become a wholly owned subsidiary of <a href="/wiki/Peel_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="Peel Group">Peel Holdings</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-liverpoolecho.co.uk_6-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-liverpoolecho.co.uk-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> \n</p>\n<h3><span id="New_Terminal_.26_Liverpool_John_Lennon_Airport_.282001.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="New_Terminal_&amp;_Liverpool_John_Lennon_Airport_(2001)">New Terminal &amp; Liverpool John Lennon Airport (2001)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Liverpool_John_Lennon_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: New Terminal &amp; Liverpool John Lennon Airport (2001)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:John_Lennon_airport.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/John_Lennon_airport.jpg/220px-John_Lennon_airport.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/John_Lennon_airport.jpg/330px-John_Lennon_airport.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/John_Lennon_airport.jpg/440px-John_Lennon_airport.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:John_Lennon_airport.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Exterior of the New Terminal, completed in 2002</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Aerial_View_of_John_Lennon_Airport_2020.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Aerial_View_of_John_Lennon_Airport_2020.jpg/220px-Aerial_View_of_John_Lennon_Airport_2020.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="238" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Aerial_View_of_John_Lennon_Airport_2020.jpg/330px-Aerial_View_of_John_Lennon_Airport_2020.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Aerial_View_of_John_Lennon_Airport_2020.jpg/440px-Aerial_View_of_John_Lennon_Airport_2020.jpg 2x" data-file-width="451" data-file-height="488" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aerial_View_of_John_Lennon_Airport_2020.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Aerial view of the airport - the passenger <a href="/wiki/Airport_terminal" title="Airport terminal">terminal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Parking_lot" title="Parking lot">parking</a> and general aviation <a href="/wiki/Hangar" title="Hangar">hangars</a> (in the top-right corner).</div></div></div>\n<p>In 2000, work on a \xc2\xa342.5 million passenger terminal began, tripling its size and passenger capacity, completed in 2002 and opened by <a href="/wiki/Her_Majesty_The_Queen_Elizabeth_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Her Majesty The Queen Elizabeth II">Her Majesty, The Queen</a>. There have since been further extensions to the airport terminal and airside. The airport\'s strategy is to cater largely for \'<a href="/wiki/Low-cost_carrier" title="Low-cost carrier">low cost</a>\' operators, and consequently the layout of the terminal and <a href="/wiki/Gate_(airport)" title="Gate (airport)">gates</a> requires passengers to walk unprotected from the weather to and from passenger aircraft.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>In 2001, 21 years after his death, the airport was renamed in honour of <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles" title="The Beatles">the Beatles</a>\' <a href="/wiki/John_Lennon" title="John Lennon">John Lennon</a>, becoming the first airport in the UK to be named after an individual.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> A 7&#160;ft (2.1&#160;m) tall bronze statue stands overlooking the <a href="/wiki/Check-in" title="Check-in">check-in</a> hall. On the roof is painted the airport\'s motto, a line from Lennon\'s song "<a href="/wiki/Imagine_(John_Lennon_song)" title="Imagine (John Lennon song)">Imagine</a>": "Above us, only sky."<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2005 the <i><a href="/wiki/Yellow_Submarine_(Liverpool)" class="mw-redirect" title="Yellow Submarine (Liverpool)">Yellow Submarine</a></i>, a large-scale work of art, was installed on a <a href="/wiki/Traffic_island" title="Traffic island">traffic island</a> at the entrance to the airport. A permanent exhibition of <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles_in_India" title="The Beatles in India">The Beatles in India</a>\'s photographs made in 1968 at the Ashram of <a href="/wiki/Maharishi_Mahesh_Yogi" title="Maharishi Mahesh Yogi">Maharishi Mahesh Yogi</a>, (founder of the <a href="/wiki/Transcendental_Meditation" title="Transcendental Meditation">Transcendental Meditation</a> technique), by <a href="/wiki/Paul_Saltzman" title="Paul Saltzman">Paul Saltzman</a> can be seen above the retail units in the departure lounge.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> \n</p><p>2005 also saw the construction of a brand-new apron, exclusively for <a href="/wiki/EasyJet" title="EasyJet">EasyJet</a>, to the east of the terminal with six stands and a pier with six boarding gates.\n</p><p>In September 2006 reconstruction started on the main runway and taxiways. This was the first time the runway had been reconstructed (as opposed to resurfaced) since it was opened in 1966. This work was completed in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-surface_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-surface-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> In addition to runway and shoulder work was the upgrade of the 40-year-old airfield group lighting with a new system, intended to upgrade the runway to <a href="/wiki/Category_III_approach" class="mw-redirect" title="Category III approach">ILS Category III</a> standards.<sup id="cite_ref-surface_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-surface-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2007 construction of a multi-level car park<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> and a budget <a href="/wiki/Hampton_by_Hilton_Liverpool_John_Lennon_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Hampton by Hilton Liverpool John Lennon Airport">Hampton by Hilton Liverpool/John Lennon Airport</a> started. The hotel opened in October 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> In June 2010 <a href="/wiki/Vancouver_Airport_Services" class="mw-redirect" title="Vancouver Airport Services">Vancouver Airport Services</a> announced that it reached an agreement with <a href="/wiki/The_Peel_Group" title="The Peel Group">The Peel Group</a> to acquire 65% share in its airports, including Liverpool.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> Airside improvements include additional retail units and a more advanced security area aiming at reducing waiting times, completed in autumn 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>April 2014 saw Peel repurchase the 65% stake it had sold in the airport giving it 100% ownership once more.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> In March 2016, Peel sold a 20% stake in the airport to Liverpool City Council for a reported \xc2\xa312m. This valued the airport at \xc2\xa360m.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> From 2019 to early 2020, the airport completed some renovation works which made it even easier to get around and also more aesthetically pleasing. <sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> This included changing the gate numbers from Gates 30\xe2\x80\x9343 to Gates 11\xe2\x80\x9317, in order to make the gates larger and more spacious, which also involved removing two by merging gates together. In addition, the departure hall, security hall and the entire experience throughout the airport has been altered massively by new decorations and images promoting the surrounding region. <sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Future_expansion">Future expansion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Liverpool_John_Lennon_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Future expansion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Future developments include the potential estimated \xc2\xa3100 million investments in the airport infrastructure - this includes a <a href="/wiki/Runway" title="Runway">runway</a> extension (enabling <a href="/wiki/Transatlantic_flight" title="Transatlantic flight">transatlantic</a>/long-haul flights)<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> as well as a new <a href="/wiki/Cargo" title="Cargo">cargo</a> area south of the runway, new taxiway, terminal expansion (including new food/drink outlets, larger <a href="/wiki/Security_checkpoint" title="Security checkpoint">security</a> areas as well as 3 new piers/concourses), hotel/parking expansion as well as the plans for a new <a href="/wiki/A-road" class="mw-redirect" title="A-road">A-road</a> to enhance motorway connections to the facilities.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> In addition to this, the airport also wants to build a <a href="/wiki/Nature_reserve" title="Nature reserve">nature reserve</a> on the coastal perimeter of the Oglet Shore.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> Plans also include schemes to improve public transport connections to the airport, including new <a href="/wiki/Bus_service" class="mw-redirect" title="Bus service">bus</a> and rail services to <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_South_Parkway_railway_station" title="Liverpool South Parkway railway station">South Parkway</a>. \n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminal">Terminal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Liverpool_John_Lennon_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Terminal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The single terminal at Liverpool John Lennon Airport has a capacity of 7 million passengers a year<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> and consists of an arrivals and departures hall, both connected within short walking distance of each other. There are no <a href="/wiki/Jet_bridge" title="Jet bridge">jetbridges</a> or <a href="/wiki/Moving_walkway" title="Moving walkway">travelators</a> at Liverpool, requiring passengers to walk to/from the departure/arrival halls and gates. \n</p><p>Airside, the terminal is divided into the east and west aprons. The, you walk straight through to Border Control via a sheltered <a href="/wiki/Footpath" title="Footpath">footpath</a> or straight into it from Gates 1\xe2\x80\x933. From the east apron, you walk through a long corridor, which passes the Departures Lounge and has glass walls, with views of the apron, and down a flight of stairs into Border Control.\n</p><p>There are also a number of retail and food outlets located within the airport including a duty free section for departing passengers. Arrivals facilities are limited. <sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Airport_directors">Airport directors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Liverpool_John_Lennon_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Airport directors">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Captain Harold James Andrews was appointed as the first Airport Manager in July 1932, and he was effectively the first full-time professional co-ordinator for the whole project. Jack Chadwick took over many of the management functions post-war until 1961. That year there was a traffic increase of 42%, attributed to the first airport marketing campaign initiated by the new Airport Director, Wing Commander H.W.G.Andrews.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the late 1960s, Brian Trunkfield MBE was a much-respected Assistant Director, and Keith Porter took over as Airport Director in the days when The Beatles were regular passengers.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> Chris Preece, a former executive of <a href="/wiki/British_Aerospace" title="British Aerospace">British Aerospace</a>, was Airport Director during much of the British Aerospace years of ownership, replaced by Rod Rufus and then Rod Hill, who brought in Direct Holidays, part of the <a href="/wiki/MyTravel_Group" title="MyTravel Group">MyTravel Group</a> on a commercial deal which was to prove the market for <a href="/wiki/EasyJet" title="EasyJet">easyJet</a>. <a href="/wiki/Neil_Pakey" title="Neil Pakey">Neil Pakey</a> took over as Managing Director in 2002, taking the airport through its major passenger growth years.\n</p><p>On selling the airport to Vancouver Airport Services in 2010, the former Operations Director for Vancouver Airport, Craig Richmond, took over, and on 1 March 2013, Matthew Thomas, also from Vancouver Airport Services (by then renamed Vantage Airport Group), was appointed to the role.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> Andrew Cornish held the CEO position from September 2014 until the end of June 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> John Irving became the new CEO with effect from 12 March 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> \n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Airlines_and_destinations">Airlines and destinations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Liverpool_John_Lennon_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Airlines and destinations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The following airlines operate regular scheduled and charter flights to and from Liverpool:<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable sortable" style="font-size:95%"><tbody><tr><th>Airlines</th><th class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Liverpool_John_Lennon_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Ground transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Liverpool_south_parkway.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Liverpool_south_parkway.jpg/220px-Liverpool_south_parkway.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Liverpool_south_parkway.jpg/330px-Liverpool_south_parkway.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Liverpool_south_parkway.jpg/440px-Liverpool_south_parkway.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Liverpool_south_parkway.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Liverpool_South_Parkway_railway_station" title="Liverpool South Parkway railway station">Liverpool South Parkway railway station</a> was built to improve links to the airport</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:350125_and_158780_at_Liverpool_South_Parkway.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/350125_and_158780_at_Liverpool_South_Parkway.JPG/220px-350125_and_158780_at_Liverpool_South_Parkway.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/350125_and_158780_at_Liverpool_South_Parkway.JPG/330px-350125_and_158780_at_Liverpool_South_Parkway.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/350125_and_158780_at_Liverpool_South_Parkway.JPG/440px-350125_and_158780_at_Liverpool_South_Parkway.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4320" data-file-height="3240" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:350125_and_158780_at_Liverpool_South_Parkway.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Long-distance trains from <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_South_Parkway_railway_station" title="Liverpool South Parkway railway station">Liverpool South Parkway</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Liverpool John Lennon Airport is within <a href="/wiki/Merseytravel" title="Merseytravel">Merseytravel</a> Area C, for local public transport tickets. <a href="/wiki/Plusbus" title="Plusbus">Plusbus</a> tickets are also available. The <a href="/wiki/Arriva_North_West" title="Arriva North West">Arriva North West</a> 80A &amp; 86A route to/from <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_city_centre" title="Liverpool city centre">Liverpool city centre</a> is now the way to <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_South_Parkway_railway_station" title="Liverpool South Parkway railway station">Liverpool South Parkway</a> and <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_One_bus_station" title="Liverpool One bus station">Liverpool One bus station</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Road">Road</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Liverpool_John_Lennon_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Road">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The airport has several on-site car-parks<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> and is accessible from the <a href="/wiki/A533_road" title="A533 road">A533</a> / <a href="/wiki/Silver_Jubilee_Bridge" title="Silver Jubilee Bridge">Runcorn Widnes Bridge</a> to the south, and from the <a href="/wiki/M57_motorway" title="M57 motorway">M57</a> and <a href="/wiki/A5300_road" title="A5300 road">Knowsley Expressway</a> to the north.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rail">Rail</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Liverpool_John_Lennon_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Rail">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The nearest station is the <a href="/wiki/Merseyrail" title="Merseyrail">Merseyrail</a> <a href="/wiki/Hunts_Cross_railway_station" title="Hunts Cross railway station">Hunts Cross</a> at 2.2 miles away, which is served by a direct bus service to the airport by the <a href="/wiki/Arriva_North_West" title="Arriva North West">Arriva North West</a> 89 service. Merseytravel replaced Garston and Allerton stations with <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_South_Parkway_railway_station" title="Liverpool South Parkway railway station">Liverpool South Parkway</a> at 2.9 miles from the airport at a cost of \xc2\xa332 million. Regular bus services, 80A &amp; 86A operate between the Airport and the station, operated by <a href="/wiki/Arriva_North_West" title="Arriva North West">Arriva North West</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bus_and_coach">Bus and coach</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Liverpool_John_Lennon_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Bus and coach">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Regular bus services link the airport with surrounding urban areas. Most buses that run to the airport are operated by <a href="/wiki/Arriva_North_West" title="Arriva North West">Arriva North West</a>, they connect local urban areas to the airport such as <a href="/wiki/St_Helens,_Merseyside" title="St Helens, Merseyside">St Helens</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bootle" title="Bootle">Bootle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Halewood" title="Halewood">Halewood</a>, <a href="/wiki/Runcorn" title="Runcorn">Runcorn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Widnes" title="Widnes">Widnes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Huyton" title="Huyton">Huyton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Garston,_Liverpool" title="Garston, Liverpool">Garston</a> and <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_City_Centre" class="mw-redirect" title="Liverpool City Centre">Liverpool City Centre</a> <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_One_bus_station" title="Liverpool One bus station">Liverpool One bus station</a><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> Arriva operates a 24-hour 86A service to the airport from Liverpool city centre via Penny Lane and <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_South_Parkway_railway_station" title="Liverpool South Parkway railway station">Liverpool South Parkway</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Merseytravel" title="Merseytravel">Merseytravel</a> also runs a service from the airport (3A/3B) which terminates at Huyton Industrial Estate, the service is operated by HTL Buses. In 2018 <a href="/wiki/ArrivaClick" title="ArrivaClick">ArrivaClick</a> commenced servicing the airport.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Facilities">Facilities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Liverpool_John_Lennon_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Facilities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hotels">Hotels</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Liverpool_John_Lennon_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Hotels">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:John_lennon_airport_hilton.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/John_lennon_airport_hilton.jpg/220px-John_lennon_airport_hilton.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/John_lennon_airport_hilton.jpg/330px-John_lennon_airport_hilton.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/John_lennon_airport_hilton.jpg/440px-John_lennon_airport_hilton.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3456" data-file-height="2304" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:John_lennon_airport_hilton.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Hampton by Hilton Liverpool John Lennon Airport</div></div></div>\n<p>The original terminal building dating from the late 1930s, famously seen on 1960s television footage with its terraces packed with <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles" title="The Beatles">Beatles</a> fans, was left derelict for over a decade after being replaced in 1986. It was renovated and adapted to become a hotel, opened for business in 2001, preserving its <a href="/wiki/Listed_building" title="Listed building">Grade II listed</a> <a href="/wiki/Art_Deco" title="Art Deco">Art Deco</a> style. It was part of the <a href="/wiki/Marriott_Hotels_%26_Resorts" title="Marriott Hotels &amp; Resorts">Marriott</a> chain of hotels, but later the <a href="/wiki/Crowne_Plaza_Liverpool_John_Lennon_Airport_Hotel" title="Crowne Plaza Liverpool John Lennon Airport Hotel">Crowne Plaza Liverpool John Lennon Airport Hotel</a> after a renovation in August 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-fola_13-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fola-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Hampton by Hilton Liverpool/John Lennon Airport is one of four <a href="/wiki/Hilton_Worldwide" title="Hilton Worldwide">Hilton Worldwide</a> hotels in Liverpool. It is situated directly opposite the main terminal building, and is the second largest hotel serving the complex after the Crowne Plaza.<sup id="cite_ref-hilton1_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hilton1-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>  The hotel was constructed as part of a \xc2\xa337 million development by <a href="/wiki/Peel_Holdings" class="mw-redirect" title="Peel Holdings">Peel Holdings</a> at John Lennon Airport (which also included a <a href="/wiki/Multi-storey_car_park" class="mw-redirect" title="Multi-storey car park">multi-storey car park</a>), the Hampton by Hilton Liverpool/John Lennon Airport is also the first hotel to be built actually attached to the airport\'s terminal building.<sup id="cite_ref-hilton2_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hilton2-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Accidents_and_incidents">Accidents and incidents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Liverpool_John_Lennon_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Accidents and incidents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li>On 20 July 1965 <a href="/wiki/Vickers_Viscount" title="Vickers Viscount">Vickers Viscount</a> G-AMOL of <a href="/wiki/Cambrian_Airways" title="Cambrian Airways">Cambrian Airways</a> <a href="/wiki/Cambrian_Airways_Liverpool_crash" title="Cambrian Airways Liverpool crash">crashed on approach</a> from <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Man_Airport" title="Isle of Man Airport">Isle of Man Airport</a>, killing both crew members.<sup id="cite_ref-ASN200765_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ASN200765-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>On 8 December 1983 Trans Europe Air Charter <a href="/wiki/Cessna_Citation_I" title="Cessna Citation I">Cessna Citation I</a> G-UESS from Liverpool <a href="/wiki/Stornoway_plane_crash" class="mw-redirect" title="Stornoway plane crash">crashed off the coast of Stornoway</a> killing all eight passengers and two crew members.<sup id="cite_ref-G-UESS_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-G-UESS-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>On 10 May 2001 <a href="/wiki/Spanair" title="Spanair">Spanair</a> Flight 3203 (<a href="/wiki/McDonnell_Douglas_MD-83" class="mw-redirect" title="McDonnell Douglas MD-83">McDonnell Douglas MD-83</a> EC-FXI) was substantially damaged when the starboard undercarriage collapsed on landing. All 51 people on board evacuated via the escape slides. It was repaired and returned to service.<sup id="cite_ref-MD-83_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MD-83-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>On 11 December 2019, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Gordon_(rugby_league)" title="Michael Gordon (rugby league)">Michael Gordon</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Bombardier_Global_6000" class="mw-redirect" title="Bombardier Global 6000">Bombardier Global 6000</a> private jet over ran the runway. This caused the airport to close for 18 hours, and flights were either cancelled or diverted to <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Airport" title="Manchester Airport">Manchester Airport</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Liverpool_John_Lennon_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li>The <a href="/wiki/Yellow_Submarine_(sculpture)" title="Yellow Submarine (sculpture)"><i>Yellow Submarine</i> sculpture</a>, previously displayed in Liverpool\'s <a href="/wiki/Royal_Albert_Dock,_Liverpool" title="Royal Albert Dock, Liverpool">Albert Dock</a>, is now outside the airport entrance.</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Bibliography">Bibliography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Liverpool_John_Lennon_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Bibliography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li>Phil Butler <i>Liverpool Airport - an Illustrated History</i>.
